<li id="cite_note-23"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-23">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">According to <a href="#CITEREFEl-Bizri2006">El-Bizri 2006</a>, p. 369, Avicenna was "of Persian descent". According to <a href="#CITEREFKhalidi2005">Khalidi 2005</a>, p. xviii, Avicenna was "born of Persian parentage". According to <a href="#CITEREFCopleston1993">Copleston 1993</a>, p. 190, Avicenna was "Persian by birth". <a href="#CITEREFGutas2014">Gutas 2014</a>, pp. xi, 310, mentions Avicenna as an example for "Persian-born authors" and speaks of "presumed Persian origins" for Avicenna. <a href="#CITEREFGlickLiveseyWallis2005">Glick, Livesey &amp; Wallis 2005</a>, p. 256, states "An ethnic Persian, he[Avicenna] was born in Kharmaithen, near Bukhara".</span>

<li id="cite_note-78"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-78">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">See a discussion of this in connection with an analytic take on the philosophy of mind in: <a href="/wiki/Nader_El-Bizri" title="Nader El-Bizri">Nader El-Bizri</a>, 'Avicenna and the Problem of Consciousness', in <i>Consciousness and the Great Philosophers</i>, eds. <li id="cite_note-79"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-79">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Ibn Sina, <i>الفن السادس من الطبيعيات من كتاب الشفاء القسم الأول</i> (Beirut, Lebanon.: M.A.J.D Enterprise Universitaire d'Etude et de Publication S.A.R.L)
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r996844942" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p><span title="Arabic-language text"><span dir="rtl" lang="ar">يجب أن يتوهم الواحد منا كأنه خلق دفعةً وخلق كاملاً لكنه حجب بصره عن مشاهدة الخارجات وخلق يهوى في هواء أو خلاء هوياً لا يصدمه فيه قوام الهواء صدماً ما يحوج إلى أن يحس وفرق بين أعضائه فلم تتلاق ولم تتماس ثم يتأمل هل أنه يثبت وجود ذاته ولا يشكك في إثباته لذاته موجوداً ولا يثبت مع ذلك طرفاً من أعضائه ولا باطناً من أحشائه ولا قلباً ولا دماغاً ولا شيئاً من الأشياء من خارج بل كان يثبت ذاته ولا يثبت لها طولاً ولا عرضاً ولا عمقاً ولو أنه أمكنه في تلك الحالة أن يتخيل يداً أو عضواً آخر  لم يتخيله جزء من ذاته ولا  شرطاً في ذاته وأنت تعلم أن المثبت غير الذي لم يثبت والمقربه غير الذي لم يقربه فإذن للذات التي أثبت وجودها خاصية على أنها هو بعينه غير جسمه وأعضائه التي لم تثبت فإذن المثبت له سبيل إلى أن يثبته على وجود النفس شيئاً غير الجسم بل غير جسم وأنه عارف به مستشعر له وإن كان ذاهلاً عنه يحتاج إلى أن يقرع عصاه.</span></span></p><div class="templatequotecite">— <cite>Ibn Sina, Kitab Al-Shifa, On the Soul</cite></div></blockquote></span>
</li>

<li id="cite_note-102"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-102">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Jack Zupko, "John Buridan" in <a href="/wiki/Stanford_Encyclopedia_of_Philosophy" title="Stanford Encyclopedia of Philosophy">Stanford Encyclopedia of Philosophy</a>, 2014
(<a class="external text" href="http://plato.stanford.edu/entries/buridan/notes.html#48" rel="nofollow">fn. 48</a>)
"We do not know precisely where Buridan got the idea of impetus, but a less sophisticated notion of impressed forced can be found in Avicenna's doctrine of mayl (inclination). In this he was possibly influenced by Philoponus, who was developing the Stoic notion of hormé (impulse). For discussion, see Zupko (1997) ['What Is the Science of the Soul? A Case Study in the Evolution of Late Medieval Natural Philosophy,' Synthese, 110(2): 297–334]."</span>

This was 'Abu Ali al-Husain ibn Abdallah ibn Sina (980–1037), called Avicenna in the West, the greatest physician of Islam. ... Many of his observations on chemistry are included in the <i>Kitab al-Shifa</i>, the "Book of the Remedy". In the physical section of this work he discusses the formation of minerals, which he classifies into stones, fusible substances, sulfurs, and salts. Mercury is classified with the fusible substances, metals</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+Historical+Background+of+Chemistry&amp;rft.pages=70&amp;rft.pub=Courier+Dover+Publications&amp;rft.date=1971&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-486-61053-5&amp;rft.aulast=Leicester&amp;rft.aufirst=Henry+Marshall&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DaJZVQnqcwv4C%26pg%3DPA70&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AAvicenna"></span></span>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Secondary_literature">Secondary literature</span></h3>
<ul><li><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFAfnan1958"><a href="/wiki/Soheil_Afnan" title="Soheil Afnan">Afnan, Soheil M.</a> (1958). <a class="external text" href="https://archive.org/details/avicennahislifea033070mbp" rel="nofollow"><i>Avicenna: His Life and Works</i></a>. London: G. Allen &amp; Unwin. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/OCLC_(identifier)" title="OCLC (identifier)">OCLC</a> <a class="external text" href="//www.worldcat.org/oclc/31478971" rel="nofollow">31478971</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Avicenna%3A+His+Life+and+Works&amp;rft.place=London&amp;rft.pub=G.+Allen+%26+Unwin&amp;rft.date=1958&amp;rft_id=info%3Aoclcnum%2F31478971&amp;rft.aulast=Afnan&amp;rft.aufirst=Soheil+M.&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Farchive.org%2Fdetails%2Favicennahislifea033070mbp&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AAvicenna"></span></li></ul>
<dl><dd><dl><dd>This is, on the whole, an informed and good account of the life and accomplishments of one of the greatest influences on the development of thought both Eastern and Western. ... It is not as philosophically thorough as the works of D. Saliba, A.M. Goichon, or L. Gardet, but it is probably the best essay in English on this important thinker of the Middle Ages. (Julius R. Weinberg, <i>The Philosophical Review</i>, Vol. 69, No. 2, Apr. 1960, pp. 255–259)</dd></dl></dd></dl>
<ul><li><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFGoodman2006"><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Lenn_Evan_Goodman&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Lenn Evan Goodman (page does not exist)">Goodman, Lenn E.</a> (2006). <span class="cs1-lock-registration" title="Free registration required"><a class="external text" href="https://archive.org/details/avicenna00good" rel="nofollow"><i>Avicenna</i></a></span> (Updated ed.). Cornell University Press. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-415-01929-3" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-415-01929-3"><bdi>978-0-415-01929-3</bdi></a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Avicenna&amp;rft.edition=Updated&amp;rft.pub=Cornell+University+Press&amp;rft.date=2006&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-415-01929-3&amp;rft.aulast=Goodman&amp;rft.aufirst=Lenn+E.&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Farchive.org%2Fdetails%2Favicenna00good&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AAvicenna"></span></li></ul>
<dl><dd><dl><dd>This is a distinguished work which stands out from, and above, many of the books and articles which have been written in this century on Avicenna (Ibn Sīnā) (980–1037). It has two main features on which its distinction as a major contribution to Avicennan studies may be said to rest: the first is its clarity and readability; the second is the comparative approach adopted by the author. ... (Ian Richard Netton, <i>Journal of the Royal Asiatic Society</i>, Third Series, Vol. 4, No. 2, July 1994, pp. 263–264)</dd></dl></dd></dl>
<ul><li><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation journal cs1">Gutas, Dimitri (1987). "Avicenna's maḏhab, with an Appendix on the question of his date of birth". <i>Quaderni di Studi Arabi</i>. <b>5–6</b>: 323–336.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Quaderni+di+Studi+Arabi&amp;rft.atitle=Avicenna%27s+ma%E1%B8%8Fhab%2C+with+an+Appendix+on+the+question+of+his+date+of+birth&amp;rft.volume=5%E2%80%936&amp;rft.pages=323-336&amp;rft.date=1987&amp;rft.aulast=Gutas&amp;rft.aufirst=Dimitri&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AAvicenna"></span></li>

<li><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1 cs1-prop-foreign-lang-source" id="CITEREFStrohmaier2006"><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Gotthard_Strohmaier&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Gotthard Strohmaier (page does not exist)">Strohmaier, Gotthard</a> (2006). <i>Avicenna</i> (in German). C.H. Beck. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-3-406-54134-6" title="Special:BookSources/978-3-406-54134-6"><bdi>978-3-406-54134-6</bdi></a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Avicenna&amp;rft.pub=C.H.+Beck&amp;rft.date=2006&amp;rft.isbn=978-3-406-54134-6&amp;rft.aulast=Strohmaier&amp;rft.aufirst=Gotthard&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AAvicenna"></span></li></ul>
<dl><dd><dl><dd>This German publication is both one of the most comprehensive general introductions to the life and works of the philosopher and physician Avicenna (Ibn Sīnā, d. 1037) and an extensive and careful survey of his contribution to the history of science. Its author is a renowned expert in Greek and Arabic medicine who has paid considerable attention to Avicenna in his recent studies. ... (Amos Bertolacci, <i>Isis</i>, Vol. 96, No. 4, December 2005, p. 649)</dd></dl></dd></dl>

</div></td></tr></tbody></table><div></div></td></tr></tbody></table><div></div></td></tr><tr><td class="navbox-abovebelow" colspan="2"><div>Contemporary Persian and Classical Persian are the same language, but writers since 1900 are classified as contemporary. At one time, Persian was a common cultural language of much of the non-Arabic Islamic world.  Today it is the official language of <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tajikistan" title="Tajikistan">Tajikistan</a> and one of the two official languages of <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a>.</div></td></tr></tbody></table></div>
